Rule also says immigrant children can be transported across the country together with adult strangers "if separate transportation is impractical or unavailable."
New rule also seeks to get around the current requirement that immigrant children be held in **licensed** childcare facilities by "creating an alternative federal licensing scheme for such detention."

Admin is also arguing that the definition of an "influx" of immigrant youth into the country means they should be allowed a more flexible timeline for putting them in an age-appropriate environment rather than the current 3-5 day timeline.
The admin is also seeking to broaden the definition of an "emergency" that would allow them to delay placing an immigrant child in an age-appropriate environment, feeding them meals/snacks, or allow other "noncompliance on a temporary basis."
DHS also says they will treat any undocumented person they encounter who is younger than 18 years old and who does not have a parent in the country as "unaccompanied" and will transfer them to HHS for indefinite detention.
Among the changes, DHS will no longer release immigrant children to live with a sibling, grandparent or other relative, and will only allow release to a parent or legal guardian.
